<span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12265" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12265</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12265" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12265" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Discovery of an ultra-young stellar &quot;snake&quot; with two dissolving cores in  the solar neighborhood\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Tian%2C+H">Hai-Jun Tian</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 6 pages, 4 figures, 1 table, submitted on ApJL\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Astrophysics of Galaxies (astro-ph.GA)</span>; Solar and Stellar Astrophysics (astro-ph.SR)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">In this Letter we report the discovery of an ultra-young (only 30-40\\,Myr)\nquasi-tidal tail (dubbed a stellar "snake") nearby the region of Orion complex\nfrom {\\it Gaia} DR2. The average distance of this structure is about 310\\,pc\nfrom the Sun. Both the length and width are over 200\\,pc, but the thickness is\nonly about 80\\,pc. Oddly it has only one tail. Its head includes two dissolving\ncores, which can be clearly distinguished in the 6D phase space. The two cores\nare probably broken from an open cluster of initially thousands of members with\na total mass of larger than 2000$M_{\\odot}$ in the same stellar population.\nThis population is so young (an order of magnitude younger than the ages of any\npreviously known tidal tails) that it can not be well explained with the\nclassical theory of tidal tails. In addition, we check the theory of mass\nsegregation, but do not find any strong evidence for this theory within 125\\,pc\nfrom the cluster center. Our finding challenges the current theory of the\nformation and evolution of tidal tails. Its age is well consistent with the\nhistory of the Gould Belt. So it may fill the observational gap between the\nhistory of the Gould Belt and the star formation near the Orion complex.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item2">[2]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12275" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12275</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12275" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12275" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Is diffuse intracluster light a good tracer of the galaxy cluster matter  distribution?\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Sampaio-Santos%2C+H">H. Sampaio-Santos</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Zhang%2C+Y">Y. Zhang</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Ogando%2C+R+L+C">R. L. C. Herner</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Hilton%2C+M">M. Hilton</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Choi%2C+A">A. Choi</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Gatti%2C+M">M. Gatti</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Gruen%2C+D">D. Gruen</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Hoyle%2C+B">B. Hoyle</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Rau%2C+M+M">M. M. Rau</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=De+Vicente%2C+J">J. De Vicente</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Zuntz%2C+J">J. Zuntz</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Abbott%2C+T+M+C">T. M. C. Abbott</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Aguena%2C+M">M. Aguena</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Allam%2C+S">S. Allam</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Annis%2C+J">J. Annis</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Avila%2C+S">S. Avila</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Bertin%2C+E">E. Bertin</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Brooks%2C+D">D. Brooks</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Burke%2C+D+L">D. L. Burke</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Kind%2C+M+C">M. Carrasco Kind</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Carretero%2C+J">J. Carretero</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Chang%2C+C">C. Chang</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Costanzi%2C+M">M. Costanzi</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=da+Costa%2C+L+N">L. N. da Costa</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Diehl%2C+H+T">H. T. Diehl</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Doel%2C+P">P. Doel</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Everett%2C+S">S. Everett</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Evrard%2C+A+E">A. E. Evrard</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Flaugher%2C+B">B. Flaugher</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Fosalba%2C+P">P. Fosalba</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Frieman%2C+J">J. Frieman</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Garcia-Bellido%2C+J">J. Garcia-Bellido</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Gaztanaga%2C+E">E. Gaztanaga</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Gerdes%2C+D+W">D. W. Gerdes</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Gruendl%2C+R+A">R. A. Gruendl</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Gschwend%2C+J">J. Gschwend</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Gutierrez%2C+G">G. Gutierrez</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Hinton%2C+S+R">S. R. Hinton</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Hollowood%2C+D+L">D. L. Hollowood</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Honscheid%2C+K">K. Honscheid</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=James%2C+D+J">D. J. James</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Jarvis%2C+M">M. Jarvis</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Jeltema%2C+T">T. Jeltema</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Kuehn%2C+K">K. Kuehn</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Kuropatkin%2C+N">N. Kuropatkin</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Lahav%2C+O">O. Lahav</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Maia%2C+M+A+G">M. A. G. Maia</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=March%2C+M">M. March</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Marshall%2C+J+L">J. L. Marshall</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Miquel%2C+R">R. Miquel</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Palmese%2C+A">A. Palmese</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Paz-Chinchon%2C+F">F. Paz-Chinchon</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Plazas%2C+A+A">A. A. Plazas</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Sanchez%2C+E">E. Sanchez</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Santiago%2C+B">B. Santiago</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Scarpine%2C+V">V. Scarpine</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Schubnell%2C+M">M. Schubnell</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Smith%2C+M">M. Smith</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Suchyta%2C+E">E. Suchyta</a>,  et al. (4 additional authors not shown)\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Astrophysics of Galaxies (astro-ph.GA)</span>; Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics (astro-ph.CO)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">We explore the relation between diffuse intracluster light (central galaxy\nincluded) and the galaxy cluster (baryonic and dark) matter distribution using\na sample of 528 clusters at $0.2\\leq z \\leq 0.35$ found in the Dark Energy\nSurvey (DES) Year 1 data. The surface brightness of the diffuse light shows an\nincreasing dependence on cluster total mass at larger radius, and appears to be\nself-similar with a universal radial dependence after scaling by cluster\nradius.We also compare the diffuse light radial profiles to the cluster\n(baryonic and dark) matter distribution measured through weak lensing and find\nthem to be comparable. The IllustrisTNG galaxy formation simulation offers\nfurther insight into the connection between diffuse stellar mass and cluster\nmatter distributions -- the simulation radial profile of the diffuse stellar\ncomponent does not have a similar slope with the total cluster matter content,\nalthough that of the cluster satellite galaxies does. Regardless of the radial\ntrends, the amount of diffuse stellar mass has a low-scatter scaling relation\nwith cluster\'s total mass in the simulation, out-performing the total stellar\nmass of cluster satellite galaxies. We conclude that there is no consistent\nevidence on whether or not diffuse light is a faithful radial tracer of the\ncluster matter distribution. Nevertheless, both observational and simulation\nresults reveal that diffuse light is an excellent indicator of the cluster\'s\ntotal mass.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item3">[3]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12276" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12276</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12276" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12276" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> GalaxyNet: Connecting galaxies and dark matter haloes with deep neural  networks and reinforcement learning in large volumes\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Moster%2C+B+P">Benjamin P. Moster</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Naab%2C+T">Thorsten Naab</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Lindstr%C3%B6m%2C+M">Magnus Lindstr&#xf6;m</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=O%27Leary%2C+J+A">Joseph A. O&#x27;Leary</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 21 pages, 21 figures, 6 tables, submitted\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Astrophysics of Galaxies (astro-ph.GA)</span>; Data Analysis, Statistics and Probability (physics.data-an)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">We present the novel wide &amp; deep neural network GalaxyNet, which connects the\nproperties of galaxies and dark matter haloes, and is directly trained on\nobserved galaxy statistics using reinforcement learning. The most important\nhalo properties to predict stellar mass and star formation rate (SFR) are halo\nmass, growth rate, and scale factor at the time the mass peaks, which results\nfrom a feature importance analysis with random forests. We train different\nmodels with supervised learning to find the optimal network architecture.\nGalaxyNet is then trained with a reinforcement learning approach: for a fixed\nset of weights and biases, we compute the galaxy properties for all haloes and\nthen derive mock statistics (stellar mass functions, cosmic and specific SFRs,\nquenched fractions, and clustering). Comparing these statistics to observations\nwe get the model loss, which is minimised with particle swarm optimisation.\nGalaxyNet reproduces the observed data very accurately\n($\\chi_\\mathrm{red}=1.05$), and predicts a stellar-to-halo mass relation with a\nlower normalisation and shallower low-mass slope at high redshift than\nempirical models. We find that at low mass, the galaxies with the highest SFRs\nare satellites, although most satellites are quenched. The normalisation of the\ninstantaneous conversion efficiency increases with redshift, but stays constant\nabove $z\\gtrsim0.7$. Finally, we use GalaxyNet to populate a cosmic volume of\n$(5.9~\\mathrm{Gpc})^3$ with galaxies and predict the BAO signal, the bias, and\nthe clustering of active and passive galaxies up to $z=4$, which can be tested\nwith next-generation surveys, such as LSST and Euclid.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item4">[4]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12280" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12280</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12280" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12280" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Searching for Black Holes in the Outer Solar System with LSST\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Siraj%2C+A">Amir Siraj</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Loeb%2C+A">Abraham Loeb</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 4 pages, 2 figures; submitted for publication in ApJL\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">High Energy Astrophysical Phenomena (astro-ph.HE)</span>; Earth and Planetary Astrophysics (astro-ph.EP)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">Planet Nine has been proposed to potentially be a black hole in the outer\nsolar system. We investigate the accretion flares that would result from\nimpacts of small Oort cloud objects, and find that the upcoming LSST observing\nprogram will be able to either rule out or confirm Planet Nine as a black hole\nwithin a year. We also find that LSST could rule out or confirm the existence\nof trapped planet-mass black holes out to the edge of the Oort cloud,\nindirectly probing the dark matter fraction in primordial black holes and\npotentially improving upon current limits by orders of magnitude.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item5">[5]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12281" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12281</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12281" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12281" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> A PSF-based Approach to TESS High quality data Of Stellar clusters  (PATHOS) -- II. Search for exoplanets in open clusters of the southern  ecliptic hemisphere and their frequency\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Nardiello%2C+D">D. Nardiello</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Piotto%2C+G">G. Piotto</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Deleuil%2C+M">M. Deleuil</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Malavolta%2C+L">L. Malavolta</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Montalto%2C+M">M. Montalto</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Bedin%2C+L+R">L. R. Bedin</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Borsato%2C+L">L. Borsato</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Granata%2C+V">V. Granata</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Libralato%2C+M">M. Libralato</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Manthopoulou%2C+E+E">E. E. Manthopoulou</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 19 pages, 12 figures, 3 tables. Accepted for publication in MNRAS on May 20, 2020. PATHOS light curves are available at MAST as HLSP at <a href="https://archive.stsci.edu/hlsp/pathos">this https URL</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Earth and Planetary Astrophysics (astro-ph.EP)</span>; Astrophysics of Galaxies (astro-ph.GA); Solar and Stellar Astrophysics (astro-ph.SR)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">The scope of the project "A PSF-based Approach to TESS High Quality data Of\nStellar clusters" (PATHOS) is the extraction and analysis of high-precision\nlight curves of stars in stellar clusters and young associations for the\nidentification of candidate exoplanets and variable stars. The cutting-edge\ntools used in this project allow us to measure the real flux of stars in dense\nfields, minimising the effects due to contamination by neighbour sources. We\nextracted about 200 000 light curves of stars in 645 open clusters located in\nthe southern ecliptic hemisphere and observed by TESS during the first year of\nits mission. We searched for transiting signals and we found 33 objects of\ninterest, 11 of them are strong candidate exoplanets. Because of the limited\nS/N, we did not find any Earth or super-Earth. We identified two Neptune-size\nplanets orbiting stars with $R_{\\star}&lt;1.5\\,R_{\\odot}$, implying a frequency\n$f_{\\star}=1.34 \\pm 0.95\\,\\%$, consistent with the frequency around field\nstars. The 7 Jupiter candidates around stars with $R_{\\star}&lt;\\,1.5R_{\\odot}$\nimply a frequency $f_{\\star}=0.19\\pm 0.07\\,\\%$, smaller than in the field. A\nmore complete estimate of the survey completeness and false positive rate is\nneeded to confirm these results. Star-formation histories are\nbetter constrained for higher redshift galaxies, observed closer to their\nformation and quenching epochs. Taking a Monte Carlo approach, we show that\nthe former companion of S5-HVS1 was likely a main-sequence star between 1.5 and\n6 solar masses and was captured into a highly eccentric orbit with pericenter\ndistance in the range 1-10 AU and semimajor axis about $10^3$ AU. We then\nexplore the fate of the captured star. We find that the heat deposited by\ntidally excited stellar oscillation modes leads to runaway disruption if the\npericenter distance is smaller than about 3 AU. Over the past 5 Myr, its\nangular momentum has been significantly modified by orbital relaxation, which\nmay stochastically drive the pericenter inwards below 3 AU and cause tidal\ndisruption. We find an overall survival probability in the range 5% to 50%,\ndepending on the local relaxation time in the close environment of the captured\nstar, and the initial pericenter at capture. The pericenter distance of the\nsurviving star has migrated to 10-100 AU, making it potentially the most\nextreme member of the S-star cluster. Code available on GitHub at <a href="https://github.com/fcastagna/JoXSZ">this https URL</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Instrumentation and Methods for Astrophysics (astro-ph.IM)</span>; Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics (astro-ph.CO)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">The thermal Sunyaev-Zeldovich (SZ) effect and the X-ray emission offer\nseparate and highly complementary probes of the thermodynamics of the\nintracluster medium. We present JoXSZ, the first publicly available code\ndesigned to jointly fit SZ and X-ray data coming from various instruments to\nderive the thermodynamic profiles of galaxy clusters. JoXSZ follows a fully\nBayesian forward-modelling approach, accounts for the SZ calibration\nuncertainty and X-ray background level systematic. It improves upon most\nstate-of-the-art, and not publicly available, analyses because it adopts the\ncorrect Poisson-Gauss expression for the joint likelihood, makes full use of\nthe information contained in the observations, even in the case of missing\nvalues within the datasets, has a more inclusive error budget, and adopts a\nconsistent temperature across the various parts of the code, allowing for\ndifferences between X-ray and SZ gas mass weighted temperatures when required\nby the user. JoXSZ accounts for beam smearing and data analysis transfer\nfunction, accounts for the temperature and metallicity dependencies of the SZ\nand X-ray conversion factors, adopts flexible parametrization for the\nthermodynamic profiles, and on user request allows either adopting or relaxing\nthe assumption of hydrostatic equilibrium (HE). When HE holds, JoXSZ uses a\nphysical (positive) prior on the radial derivative of the enclosed mass and\nderives the mass profile and overdensity radii $r_\\Delta$. For these reasons,\nJoXSZ goes beyond simple SZ and electron density fits. We illustrate the use of\nJoXSZ by combining Chandra and NIKA data on the high-redshift cluster CL\nJ1226.9+3332. The code is written in Python, it is fully documented and the\nusers are free to customize their analysis in accordance with their needs and\nrequirements. JoXSZ is publicly available on GitHub.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item12">[12]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12336" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12336</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12336" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Exploration of the outer solar system with fast and small sailcraft\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Turyshev%2C+S+G">Slava G. Hailey</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Hare%2C+J">Jeremy Hare</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Kargaltsev%2C+O">Oleg Kargaltsev</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Mukherjee%2C+R">Reshmi Mukherjee</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> accepted to ApJ, 8 pages, 7 figures\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">High Energy Astrophysical Phenomena (astro-ph.HE)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">2HWC J1928+177 is a Galactic TeV gamma-ray source detected by the High\nAltitude Water Cherenkov (HAWC) Observatory up to ~ 56 TeV. The HAWC source,\nlater confirmed by H.E.S.S., still remains unidentified as a dark accelerator\nsince there is no apparent supernova remnant or pulsar wind nebula detected in\nthe lower energy bands. The radio pulsar PSR J1928+1746, coinciding with the\nHAWC source position, has no X-ray counterpart. Our SED modeling shows that\ninverse Compton scattering in the putative pulsar wind nebula can account for\nthe TeV emission only if the unseen nebula is extended beyond r ~ 4 [arcmin].\nAlternatively, TeV gamma rays may be produced by hadronic interactions between\nrelativistic protons from an undetected supernova remnant associated with the\nradio pulsar and a nearby molecular cloud G52.9+0.1. NuSTAR and Chandra\nobservations detected a variable X-ray point source within the HAWC error\ncircle, potentially associated with a bright IR source. The X-ray spectra can\nbe fitted with an absorbed power-law model with $N_{\\rm H} =\n(9\\pm3)\\times10^{22}$ cm$^{-2}$ and $\\Gamma_X = 1.6\\pm0.3$ and exhibit\nlong-term X-ray flux variability over the last decade. If the X-ray source,\npossibly associated with the IR source (likely an O star), is the counterpart\nof the HAWC source, it may be a new TeV gamma-ray binary powered by collisions\nbetween the pulsar wind and stellar wind. Located close to the centre of the galaxy, more metal-rich and\npotentially younger than its four companions (namely, Fornax clusters number 1,\n2, 3 and 5), it has been suggested to have experienced a different formation\nthan the other clusters in the galaxy. Here we use HST/WFC3 photometry to\ncharacterize the stellar population content of this system and shed new light\non its nature. By means of a detailed comparison of synthetic horizontal branch\nand red giant branch with the observed colour-magnitude diagrams, we find that\nthis system likely hosts stellar sub-populations characterized by a significant\niron spread up to $\\Delta$[Fe/H]$\\sim$0.4 dex and possibly by also some degree\nof He abundance variations $\\Delta$Y$\\sim0.03$. One approach to lowering consumption of ALAN in cities is\ndimming or extinguishing publicly owned outdoor lighting during overnight\nhours; however, there are few reports in the literature about the efficacy of\nthese programs. Here we report the results of one of the largest municipal\nlighting dimming experiments to date, involving $\\sim$20,000 roadway luminaires\nowned and operated by the City of Tucson, Arizona, U.S. We analyzed both\nsingle-channel and spatially resolved ground-based measurements of broadband\nnight sky radiance obtained during the tests, determining that the zenith sky\nbrightness during the tests decreased by ($-5.4\\pm0.9$)% near the city center\nand ($-3.6\\pm0.9$)% at an adjacent suburban location on nights when the output\nof the street lighting system was dimmed from 90% of its full power draw to 30%\nafter local midnight. We have performed a systematic analysis of the\nhigh-resolution X-ray spectra obtained by the Chandra observatory to determine\nthe parameters of the jets within the multitemperature model of their emission\nthat self-consistently predicts the source\'s line and continuum spectrum. The best\nfit model parameters give a jet opening angle\n$\\theta_j=5^\\circ.2^{+1.1}_{-0.6}$, an inclination to the line of sight\n$\\iota=16^\\circ.0^{+3.4}_{-1.1}$, an initial isotropic kinetic energy\n$E_1=0.3^{+3.5}_{-0.3}\\times10^{52}$ erg and a total, refreshed shock energy\n$E_{\\rm total}=0.42^{+5.6}_{-0.4}\\times10^{53}$ erg. The model fitting prefers\nan initial bulk Lorentz factor $\\Gamma_{0,1}&lt;60$, with a comparatively low\ncentral value of $\\Gamma_{0,1}=19.5$, indicating that the on-axis jet could\nhave been a `failed-GRB\' and that the associated $\\gamma$-ray emission was the\nresult of a shock-breakout or some other process.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item23">[23]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12459" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12459</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12459" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12459" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> The Herschel SPIRE Fourier Transform Spectrometer Spectral Feature  Finder I. The Spectral Feature Finder and Catalogue\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Hopwood%2C+R">R. Hopwood</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Valtchanov%2C+I">I. Valtchanov</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Spencer%2C+L+D">Locke D. Spencer</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Scott%2C+J+P">J. P. Scott</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Benson%2C+C+S">C.S. Hladczuk</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Polehampton%2C+E+T">E. T. Polehampton</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Lu%2C+N">N. Lu</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Makiwa%2C+G">G. Makiwa</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Naylor%2C+D+A">D. A. Naylor</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Gom%2C+B+G">B. G. Gom</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Noble%2C+G">G. Noble</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Griffin%2C+M+J">M. J. Griffin</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 20 pages, 8 figures, 8 tables, accepted by MNRAS March 2020\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Instrumentation and Methods for Astrophysics (astro-ph.IM)</span>; Astrophysics of Galaxies (astro-ph.GA)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">We provide a detailed description of the Herschel SPIRE Fourier Transform\nSpectrometer (FTS) Spectral Feature Finder (FF). The FF is an automated process\ndesigned to extract significant spectral features from SPIRE FTS data products.\nOptimising the number of features found in SPIRE FTS spectra is challenging.\nThe wide SPIRE FTS frequency range (447-1568 GHz) leads to many molecular\nspecies and atomic fine structure lines falling within the observed bands. As\nthe best spectral resolution of the SPIRE FTS is ~1.2 GHz, there can be\nsignificant line blending, depending on the source type. In order to find, both\nefficiently and reliably, features in spectra associated with a wide range of\nsources, the FF iteratively searches for peaks over a number of signal-to-noise\nratio (SNR) thresholds. For each threshold, newly identified features are\nrigorously checked before being added to the fitting model. At the end of each\niteration, the FF simultaneously fits the continuum and features found, with\nthe resulting residual spectrum used in the next iteration. The final FF\nproducts report the frequency of the features found and the associated SNRs.\nLine flux determination is not included as part of the FF products, as\nextracting reliable line flux from SPIRE FTS data is a complex process that\nrequires careful evaluation and analysis of the spectra on a case-by-case\nbasis. The FF results are 100% complete for features with SNR greater than 10\nand 50-70% complete at SNR of 5. The FF code and all FF products are publicly\navailable via the Herschel Science Archive.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item24">[24]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12460" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12460</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12460" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12460" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> The Herschel SPIRE Fourier Transform Spectrometer Spectral Feature  Finder II. Estimating Radial Velocity of SPIRE Spectral Observation Sources\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Scott%2C+J+P">Jeremy P. The first routine is based on\nthe identification of rotational CO emission, the second cross-correlates\ndetected features with a line template containing most of the characteristic\nlines in typical far infra-red observations. Naylor</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 15 pages (+2 appendix pages), 14 figures, 7 tables, accepted by MNRAS April 2020\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Instrumentation and Methods for Astrophysics (astro-ph.IM)</span>; Astrophysics of Galaxies (astro-ph.GA)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">The ESA Herschel Spectral and Photometric Imaging Receiver (SPIRE) Fourier\nTransform Spectrometer (FTS) Spectral Feature Finder (FF) project is an\nautomated spectral feature fitting routine developed within the SPIRE\ninstrument team to extract all prominent spectral features from all publicly\navailable SPIRE FTS observations. We present the extension of the FF to include\nthe off-axis detectors of the FTS in sparsely sampled single-pointing\nobservations, the results of which have been ingested into the catalogue. We\nalso present the results from an automated routine for identifications of the\natomic/molecular transitions that correspond to the spectral features extracted\nby the FF. We use a template of 307 atomic fine structure and molecular lines\nthat are commonly found in SPIRE FTS spectra for the cross-match. The routine\nmakes use of information provided by the line identification to search for low\nsignal-to-noise ratio features that have been excluded or missed by the\niterative FF. In total, the atomic/molecular transitions of 178,942 lines are\nidentified (corresponding to 83% of the entire FF catalogue), and an additional\n33,840 spectral lines associated with missing features from SPIRE FTS\nobservations are added to the FF catalogue.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item26">[26]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12462" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12462</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12462" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12462" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> The Herschel SPIRE Fourier Transform Spectrometer Spectral Feature  Finder IV. K-CLASH aims to study the transition of star-forming galaxies\nfrom turbulent, highly star-forming disc-like and peculiar systems at\n$z\\approx1$-$3$, to the comparatively quiescent, ordered late-type galaxies at\n$z\\approx0$, and to examine the role of clusters in the build-up of the red\nsequence since $z\\approx1$. In this paper, we describe the K-CLASH survey,\npresent the sample, and provide an overview of the K-CLASH galaxy properties.\nWe demonstrate that our sample comprises star-forming galaxies typical of their\nstellar masses and epochs, residing both in field and cluster environments. We\nconclude K-CLASH provides an ideal sample to bridge the gap between existing\nlarge integral-field spectroscopy surveys at higher and lower redshifts. We\nfind that star-forming K-CLASH cluster galaxies at intermediate redshifts have\nsystematically lower stellar masses than their star-forming counterparts in the\nfield, hinting at possible ``downsizing\'\' scenarios of galaxy growth in\nclusters at these epochs. We show that even\nthough the current and charge neutralities are initially satisfied, the current\nneutrality is eventually violated if there is an inhomogeneity, so that the\nmagnetic field is generated. By conducting ab initio two-dimensional\nparticle-in-cell simulations, we demonstrate that the magnetic field is\ngenerated as expected. In particular, focal plane attitude calibration is\nan essential optical path calibration technique that has a direct impact on\nimage quality. In this paper, a focal plane attitude detection method using\neight acquisition cameras is proposed based on the calibration requirements of\nthe wide-field telescope, LAMOST. We find the comoving number density of these objects to be\n$\\sim 2 \\times 10^{-5}$ and $8 \\times 10^{-6}Mpc^{-3}$ after correction for\ncompleteness for two redshift bins centered at $z=3.4, 4.7$. Then we compare the evolution of the corresponding number\ndensities and their stellar mass density with numerical simulations,\nsemi-analytical models, and previous observational estimates, which shows\nslight tension at higher redshifts as the models tend to underestimate the\nnumber and mass densities. Accepted for publication in MNRAS\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Astrophysics of Galaxies (astro-ph.GA)</span>; High Energy Astrophysical Phenomena (astro-ph.HE)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">The supermassive black holes (SMBHs) of narrow-line Seyfert 1 galaxies\n(NLS1s) are at the lowest end of mass function of active galactic nuclei (AGNs)\nand preferentially reside in late-type host galaxies with pseudobulges, which\nare thought to be formed by internal secular evolution. On the other hand, the\npopulation of radio-loud NLS1s presents a challenge for the relativistic jet\nparadigm that powerful radio jets are exclusively associated with very high\nmass SMBHs in elliptical hosts, which are built-up through galaxy mergers. We\ninvestigated distorted radio structures associated with the nearest gamma-ray\nemitting, radio-loud NLS1 1H 0323+342. The anomalous radio morphology consists of two different\nstructures, the inner curved structure of currently active jet and the outer\nlinear structure of low-brightness relics. Such a coexistence might be\nindicative of the stage of an established black hole binary with precession\nbefore the black holes coalesce in the galaxy merger process. 1H 0323+342 and\nother radio-loud NLS1s under galaxy interactions may be extreme objects on the\nevolutionary path from radio-quiet NLS1s to normal Seyfert galaxies with larger\nSMBHs in classical bulges through mergers and merger-induced jet phases.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item32">[32]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12527" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12527</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12527" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/ps/2005.12527" title="Download PostScript">ps</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12527" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Understanding the Fundamental Plane and the Tully Fisher Relation\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Mould%2C+J">Jeremy Mould</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> For publication in Frontiers in Astronomy and Space Sciences\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Astrophysics of Galaxies (astro-ph.GA)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">The relation between early type galaxy size, surface brightness and velocity\ndispersion, "the fundamental plane", has long been understood as resulting from\nequilibrium in their largely pressure supported stellar dynamics. The\ndissipation and feedback involved in reaching such an equilibrium through\nmerger formation of these galaxies over cosmic time can be responsible for the\norientation of the plane. We see a correlation between surface brightness\nenhancement and youth in the 6dF Galaxy Survey. Correlations of this `tilt\'\nwith stellar mass, age, concentration, shape and metallicity now point the\ndirection for further work on the resolved kinematics and structure of these\nnearby galaxies and on their initial mass function and dark matter component.\n<br />On the face of it, the Tully Fisher relation is a simpler one dimensional\nscaling relation. However, as late type galaxies have bulges as well as disks,\nand, as the surface density of disks is only standard for the more massive\ngalaxies, additional parameters are involved.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item33">[33]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12528" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12528</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12528" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12528" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> The Process of Stellar Tidal Disruption by Supermassive Black Holes. The  first pericenter passage\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Rossi%2C+E+M">Elena M. Rossi</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Stone%2C+N+C">Nicholas C. Stone</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Law-Smith%2C+J+A+P">Jamie A.P. Law-Smith</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=MacLeod%2C+M">Morgan MacLeod</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Lodato%2C+G">Giuseppe Lodato</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Dai%2C+J+L">Jane L. Dai</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Mandel%2C+I">Ilya Mandel</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> Review chapter in book: \'The Tidal Disruption of Stars by Massive Black Holes\', Space Science Reviews, Springer. Comments welcome\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">High Energy Astrophysical Phenomena (astro-ph.HE)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">Tidal disruption events (TDEs) are among the brightest transients in the\noptical, ultraviolet, and X-ray sky. These flares are set into motion when a\nstar is torn apart by the tidal field of a massive black hole, triggering a\nchain of events which is -- so far -- incompletely understood. However, the\ndisruption process has been studied extensively for almost half a century, and\nunlike the later stages of a TDE, our understanding of the disruption itself is\nreasonably well converged. In this Chapter, we review both analytical and\nnumerical models for stellar tidal disruption. Starting with relatively simple,\norder-of-magnitude physics, we review models of increasing sophistication, the\nsemi-analytic ``affine formalism,\'\' hydrodynamic simulations of the disruption\nof polytropic stars, and the most recent hydrodynamic results concerning the\ndisruption of realistic stellar models. Our review surveys the immediate\naftermath of disruption in both typical and more unusual TDEs, exploring how\nthe fate of the tidal debris changes if one considers non-main sequence stars,\ndeeply penetrating tidal encounters, binary star systems, and sub-parabolic\norbits. The stellar tidal disruption process provides the initial conditions\nneeded to model the formation of accretion flows around quiescent massive black\nholes, and in some cases may also lead to directly observable emission, for\nexample via shock breakout, gravitational waves or runaway nuclear fusion in\ndeeply plunging TDEs.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item34">[34]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12530" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12530</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12530" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/ps/2005.12530" title="Download PostScript">ps</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12530" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Smooth stochastic density field reconstruction\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Aragon-Calvo%2C+M+A">Miguel A. Aragon-Calvo</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> Submitted to MNRAS\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics (astro-ph.CO)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">We introduce a method for generating a continuous, mass-conserving and\nhigh-order differentiable density field from a discrete point distribution such\nas particles or halos from an N-body simulation or galaxies from a\nspectroscopic survey. The method consists on generating an ensemble of point\nrealizations by perturbing the original point set following the geometric\nconstraints imposed by the Delaunay tessellation in the vicinity of each point\nin the set. By computing the mean field of the ensemble we are able to\nsignificantly reduce artifacts arising from the Delaunay tessellation in poorly\nsampled regions while conserving the features in the point distribution. Our\nimplementation is based on the Delaunay Tessellation Field Estimation (DTFE)\nmethod, however other tessellation techniques are possible. The method\npresented here shares the same advantages of the DTFE method such as\nself-adaptive scale, mass conservation and continuity, while being able to\nreconstruct even the faintest structures of the point distribution usually\ndominated by artifacts in Delaunay-based methods. Additionally, we also present\npreliminary results of an application of this method to image denoising and\nartifact removal, highlighting the broad applicability of the technique\nintroduced here.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item35">[35]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12549" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12549</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12549" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12549" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Change of a Weibel-type to an Alfv&#xe9;nic shock in pair plasma by  upstream waves\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Dieckmann%2C+M+E">M E Dieckmann</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Riordan%2C+J+D">J D Riordan</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Pe%27er%2C+A">A Pe&#x27;er</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 11 pages, 10 figures, accepted for publication in Physics of Plasmas\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">High Energy Astrophysical Phenomena (astro-ph.HE)</span>; Plasma Physics (physics.plasm-ph)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">We examine with particle-in-cell (PIC) simulations how a parallel shock in\npair plasma reacts to upstream waves, which are driven by escaping downstream\nparticles. Initially, the shock is sustained in the two-dimensional simulation\nby a magnetic filamentation (beam-Weibel) instability. Escaping particles drive\nan electrostatic beam instability upstream. Modifications of the upstream\nplasma by these waves hardly affect the shock. In time, a decreasing density\nand increasing temperature of the escaping particles quench the beam\ninstability. A larger thermal energy along than perpendicular to the magnetic\nfield destabilizes the pair-Alfv\\\'en mode. In the rest frame of the upstream\nplasma, the group velocity of the growing pair-Alfv\\\'en waves is below that of\nthe shock and the latter catches up with the waves. Accumulating pair-Alfv\\\'en\nwaves gradually change the shock in the two-dimensional simulation from a\nWeibel-type shock into an Alfv\\\'enic shock with a Mach number that is about 6\nfor our initial conditions.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item36">[36]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12555" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12555</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12555" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Star formation in thin disks of spiral galaxies seen face-on\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Karachentseva%2C+V+E">V. They could form a specific class of high-energy transient events,\nwhose origin is still under discussion. The current sample of known ulGRBs\nconsists of a few tens of events which have been detected so far by the Burst\nAlert Telescope (BAT) aboard the Neil Gehrels Swift Observatory and some other\ninstruments. Comments are welcome\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Solar and Stellar Astrophysics (astro-ph.SR)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">The mass, origin and evolutionary stage of the binary system LB-1 has been\nthe subject of intense debate, following the claim that it hosts an\n$\\sim$70$M_{\\odot}$ black hole, in stark contrast with the expectations for\nstellar remnants in the Milky Way. We conducted a high-resolution,\nphase-resolved spectroscopic study of the near-infrared Paschen lines in this\nsystem, using the 3.5-m telescope at Calar Alto Observatory. We find that\nPa$\\beta$ and Pa$\\gamma$ (after proper subtraction of the stellar absorption\ncomponent) are well fitted with a standard double-peaked model, typical of disk\nemission. We measured the velocity shifts of the red and blue peaks at 28\norbital phases: the line center has an orbital motion in perfect antiphase with\nthe stellar motion, and the radial velocity amplitude ranges from 8 to 13 km/s\nfor different choices of lines and profile modelling. We interpret this curve\nas proof that the disk is tracing the orbital motion of the primary, ruling out\nthe circumbinary disk and the hierarchical triple scenarios. The phase-averaged\npeak-to-peak half-separation (proxy for the projected rotational velocity of\nthe outer disk) is $\\sim$70 km s$^{-1}$, larger than the stellar orbital\nvelocity and also inconsistent with a circumbinary disk. From those results, we\ninfer a primary mass 4--8 times higher than the secondary mass. Moreover, we\nshow that the ratio of the blue and red peaks (V/R intensity ratio) has a\nsinusoidal behaviour in phase with the secondary star, which can be interpreted\nas the effect of external irradiation by the secondary star on the outer disk.\nFinally, we briefly discuss our findings in the context of alternative\nscenarios recently proposed for LB-1. Definitive tests between alternative\nsolutions will require further astrometric data from $Gaia$.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item41">[41]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12596" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12596</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12596" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12596" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> ARCHI: pipeline for light curve extraction of CHEOPS background star\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Silva%2C+A+M">Andr&#xe9; M. In this context, the recently launched CHEOPS (ESA)\nmission promises to bring 20 ppm precision over an exposure time of 6 hours,\nwhen targeting nearby bright stars, having in mind the detailed\ncharacterization of exoplanetary systems through transit measurements. However,\nthe official CHEOPS (ESA) mission pipeline only provides photometry for the\nmain target (the central star in the field). In order to explore the potential\nof CHEOPS photometry for all stars in the field, in this paper we present\narchi, an additional open-source pipeline module{\\dag}to analyse the background\nstars present in the image. As archi uses the official Data Reduction Pipeline\ndata as input, it is not meant to be used as independent tool to process raw\nCHEOPS data but, instead, to be used as an add-on to the official pipeline. We\ntest archi using CHEOPS simulated images, and show that photometry of\nbackground stars in CHEOPS images is only slightly degraded (by a factor of 2\nto 3) with respect to the main target. This opens a potential for the use of\nCHEOPS to produce photometric time series of several close-by targets at once,\nas well as to use different stars in the image to calibrate systematic errors.\nWe also show one clear scientific application where the study of the companion\nlight curve can be important for the understanding of the contamination on the\nmain target.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item42">[42]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12616" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12616</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12616" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12616" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Spectroscopic and Photometric Periods of Six Ultracompact Accreting  Binaries\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Green%2C+M+J">Matthew J. Such binaries\ninclude two related sub-classes, AM CVn-type binaries and helium cataclysmic\nvariables, in both of which the central star is a white dwarf. We present a\nspectroscopic and photometric study of six accreting binaries with orbital\nperiods in the range of 40--70 min, including phase-resolved VLT spectroscopy\nand high-speed ULTRACAM photometry. MOA 2010-BLG-087 is co-aligned with a K-class star that\ndominates its spectrum. APEX observations and radiative transfer modelling\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Bergman%2C+P">P. Bergman</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Humphreys%2C+E+M+L">E. M. L. Humphreys</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> Accepted for publication in A&amp;A\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Solar and Stellar Astrophysics (astro-ph.SR)</span>; Astrophysics of Galaxies (astro-ph.GA)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">Here we aim to characterise submillimetre water masers at 437, 439, 471, and\n474 GHz towards a sample of evolved stars.\n<br />We used the Atacama Pathfinder Experiment (APEX) to observe submillimetre\nwater transitions and the CO (4-3) line towards 11 evolved stars. The sample\nincluded semi-regular and Mira variables, plus a red supergiant star. We\nperformed radiative transfer modelling for the water masers. We also used the\nCO observations to determine mass loss rates for the stars.\n<br />From the sample of 11 evolved stars, 7 display one or more of the masers at\n437, 439, 471, and 474 GHz. We therefore find that these masers are common in\nevolved star circumstellar envelopes. The fact that the maser lines are\ndetected near the stellar velocity indicates that they are likely to originate\nfrom the inner circumstellar envelopes of our targets. We tentatively link the\npresence of masers to the degree of variability of the target star, that is,\nmasers are more likely to be present in Mira variables than in semi-regular\nvariables. We suggest that this indicates the importance of strong shocks in\ncreating the necessary conditions for the masers. Typically, the 437 GHz line\nis the strongest maser line observed among those studied here. We cannot\nreproduce the above finding in our radiative transfer models. In general, we\nfind that maser emission is very sensitive to dust temperature in the lines\nstudied here. To produce strong maser emission, the dust temperature must be\nsignificantly lower than the gas kinetic temperature. In addition to running\ngrids of models in order to determine the optimum physical conditions for\nstrong masers in these lines, we performed smooth wind modelling for which we\ncannot reproduce the observed line shapes. This also suggests that the masers\nmust originate predominantly from the inner envelopes.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item45">[45]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12655" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12655</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12655" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12655" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> A probabilistic approach to phase calibration: I. Effects of source  structure on fringe-fitting\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Natarajan%2C+I">Iniyan Natarajan</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Deane%2C+R">Roger Deane</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=van+Bemmel%2C+I">Ilse van Bemmel</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=van+Langevelde%2C+H+J">Huib Jan van Langevelde</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Small%2C+D">Des Small</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Kettenis%2C+M">Mark Kettenis</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Paragi%2C+Z">Zsolt Paragi</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Smirnov%2C+O">Oleg Smirnov</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Szomoru%2C+A">Arpad Szomoru</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> accepted for publication in MNRAS\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Instrumentation and Methods for Astrophysics (astro-ph.IM)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">We propose a probabilistic framework for performing simultaneous estimation\nof source structure and fringe-fitting parameters in Very Long Baseline\nInterferometry (VLBI) observations. As a first step, we demonstrate this\ntechnique through the analysis of synthetic short-duration Event Horizon\nTelescope (EHT) observations of various geometric source models at 230 GHz, in\nthe presence of baseline-dependent thermal noise. We perform Bayesian parameter\nestimation and model selection between the different source models to obtain\nreliable uncertainty estimates and correlations between various source and\nfringe-fitting related model parameters. We also compare the Bayesian\nposteriors with those obtained using widely-used VLBI data reduction packages\nsuch as CASA and AIPS, by fringe-fitting 200 Monte Carlo simulations of each\nsource model with different noise realisations, to obtain distributions of the\nMaximum A Posteriori (MAP) estimates. We find that, in the presence of resolved\nasymmetric source structure and a given array geometry, the traditional\npractice of fringe-fitting with a point source model yields appreciable offsets\nin the estimated phase residuals, potentially biasing or limiting the dynamic\nrange of the starting model used for self-calibration. Simultaneously\nestimating the source structure earlier in the calibration process with formal\nuncertainties improves the precision and accuracy of fringe-fitting and\nestablishes the potential of the available data especially when there is little\nprior information. We also note the potential applications of this method to\nastrometry and geodesy for specific science cases and the planned improvements\nto the computational performance and analyses of more complex source\ndistributions.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item46">[46]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12677" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12677</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12677" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12677" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Mapping the radio to mid-infrared spectral index of Cas A: evidence for  flattening and a cooling break\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Dom%C4%8Dek%2C+V">V. Searching for high-redshift galaxies is a field of intense activity\nin modern observational cosmology that will continue to grow with future\nground-based and sky observatories. Over the last few years, a lot has been\nlearned about the high-z Universe. Aims. Despite extensive Ly-alpha Blobs (LAB)\nsurveys from low to high redshifts, giant LABs over 100 kpc have been found\nmostly at z~2-4. This redshift range is coincident with the transition epoch of\ngalactic gas-circulation processes from inflows to outflows at z~2.5-3. This\nsuggests that the formation of giant LABs may be related to a combination of\ngas inflows and outflows. Their extreme youth makes them interesting objects in\nthe study of galaxy formation as they provide insight into some of the youngest\nknown highly star forming galaxies, with only modest time investments using\nground-based telescopes. Methods. Systematic narrow-band Ly-alpha nebula\nsurveys are ongoing, but they are limited in their covered redshift range and\ntheir comoving volume. This poses a significant problem when searching for such\nrare sources. To address this problem, we developed a systematic searching\ntool, ATACAMA (A Tool for seArChing for lArge LyMan Alpha nebulae) designed to\nfind large Ly-alpha nebulae at any redshift within deep multi-wavelength\nbroad-band imaging. Results. We identified a Ly-alpha nebula candidate at\nzphot~3.3 covering an isophotal area of 29.4sq.arcsec. Its morphology shows a\nbright core and a faint core which coincides with the morphology of previously\nknown Ly-alpha blobs. The observatories targeted\na chromospheric plage region of which the spatial distribution (split between\nstrongly and weakly magnetized regions) allowed the study of linear-like\nstructures in isolation, free of contamination from background emission. Using\nthese observations in conjunction with a radiative magnetohydrodynamic 2.5D\nmodel covering the upper convection zone all the way to the corona that\nconsiders non-equilibrium ionization effects, we report the detection of an\non-disk chromospheric spicule with \\emph{ALMA} and confirm its multithermal\nnature. In addition, we discuss the strikingly high degree of similarity\nbetween chromospheric plage features observed in \\emph{ALMA}/Band6 and\n\\emph{IRIS}/\\ion{Si}{4} (also reproduced in our model) suggesting that\n\\emph{ALMA}/Band6 does not observe in the low chromosphere as previously\nthought but rather observes the upper chromospheric parts of structures such as\nspicules and other bright structures above plage at geometric heights near\ntransition region temperatures. We also show that \\emph{IRIS}/\\ion{Mg}{2} is\nnot as well correlated with \\emph{ALMA}/Band6 as was previously thought. For\nthese comparisons, we propose and employ a novel empirical method for the\ndetermination of plage regions, which seems to better isolate plage from its\nsurrounding regions as compared to other methods commonly used. We caution that\nisolating plage from its immediate surroundings must be done with care to\nmitigate stastistical bias in quantitative comparisons between different\nchromospheric observables. The spectra are\nclassified as AGN-like, HII-region-like (or SF-like), and intermediate (INT)\nspectra according to their positions on the BPT diagram. There are the\nfollowing four configurations of the radiation distributions in the\ncircumnuclear regions: 1) AGN+INT, the innermost region of the AGN-like\nradiation is surrounded by a ring of radiation of the intermediate type; 2)\nINT, the central area of radiation of the intermediate type; 3) SF+INT, the\ninner region of the HII-region-like radiation is surrounded by a ring of\nradiation of the intermediate type; and 4) SF, the HII-region-like radiation\nonly. The LINERS of configurations 1 and 2 are examined. The spaxel spectra of\nthe LINERs form a sequences on the BPT diagram. The line ratios change smoothly\nwith radius, from AGN-like at the center to HII-region-like at larger\ndistances. This is in agreement with the paradigm that the LINERs are excited\nby AGN activity. The AGN and INT radiation in the circumnuclear region is\naccompanied by an enhanced gas velocity dispersion, s_g. The radius of the area\nof the AGN and INT radiation is similar to the radius of the area with enhanced\ns_g, and the central s_g,c correlates with the luminosity of the AGN+INT area.\nWe assume that the gas velocity dispersion can serve as an indicator of the AGN\nactivity. The values of s_g,c for the SF-type centers partly overlap with those\nof the AGN-type centers. Gary</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Reeves%2C+K+K">Katharine K. Reeves</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Fleishman%2C+G+D">Gregory D. Fleishman</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Yu%2C+S">Sijie Yu</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Guo%2C+F">Fan Guo</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Krucker%2C+S">S&#xe4;m Krucker</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Lin%2C+J">Jun Lin</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Nita%2C+G">Gelu Nita</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Kong%2C+X">Xiangliang Kong</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 16 pages, 8 figures\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Solar and Stellar Astrophysics (astro-ph.SR)</span>; High Energy Astrophysical Phenomena (astro-ph.HE); Space Physics (physics.space-ph)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">In the standard model of solar flares, a large-scale reconnection current\nsheet is postulated as the central engine for powering the flare energy release\nand accelerating particles. However, where and how the energy release and\nparticle acceleration occur remain unclear due to the lack of measurements for\nthe magnetic properties of the current sheet. Here we report the measurement of\nspatially-resolved magnetic field and flare-accelerated relativistic electrons\nalong a current-sheet feature in a solar flare. The measured magnetic field\nprofile shows a local maximum where the reconnecting field lines of opposite\npolarities closely approach each other, known as the reconnection X point. The\nmeasurements also reveal a local minimum near the bottom of the current sheet\nabove the flare loop-top, referred to as a "magnetic bottle". This spatial\nstructure agrees with theoretical predictions and numerical modeling results. A\nstrong reconnection electric field of ~4000 V/m is inferred near the X point.\nThis location, however, shows a local depletion of microwave-emitting\nrelativistic electrons. These electrons concentrate instead at or near the\nmagnetic bottle structure, where more than 99% of them reside at each instant.\nOur observations suggest that the loop-top magnetic bottle is likely the\nprimary site for accelerating and/or confining the relativistic electrons.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item51">[51]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12758" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12758</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12758" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12758" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Axisymmetric equilibrium models for magnetised neutron stars in  Scalar-Tensor Theories\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Soldateschi%2C+J">J. Del Zanna</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> accepted for publication by A&amp;A\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">High Energy Astrophysical Phenomena (astro-ph.HE)</span>; General Relativity and Quantum Cosmology (gr-qc)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">Among the possible extensions of General Relativity that have been put\nforward in order to address some long standing issues in our understanding of\nthe Universe, Scalar-Tensor Theories have received a lot of attention for their\nsimplicity. Interestingly, some of these predict a potentially observable\nnon-linear phenomenon, known as \\textit{spontaneous scalarisation}, in the\npresence of highly compact matter distributions, like the case of neutron\nstars. Neutron stars are ideal laboratories to investigate the properties of\nmatter under extreme conditions, and in particular they are known to harbour\nthe strongest magnetic fields in the Universe. Here, for the first time, we\npresent a detailed study of magnetised neutron stars in Scalar-Tensor Theories.\nFirst, we show that the formalism developed for the study of magnetised neutron\nstars in General Relativity, based on the \\textit{eXtended Conformally Flat\nCondition}, can easily be extended in the presence of a non-minimally coupled\nscalar field, retaining many of its numerical advantages. We then carry out a\nstudy of the parameter space considering the two extreme geometries of purely\ntoroidal and purely poloidal magnetic fields, varying both the strength of the\nmagnetic field and the intensity of scalarisation. We compare our results with\nmagnetised general-relativistic solutions and un-magnetised scalarised\nsolutions, showing how the mutual interplay between magnetic and scalar fields\naffect the magnetic and the scalarisation properties of neutron stars. In\nparticular, we focus our discussion on magnetic deformability, maximum mass and\nrange of scalarisation.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item52">[52]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12761" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12761</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12761" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12761" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> iDQ: Statistical Inference of Non-Gaussian Noise with Auxiliary Degrees  of Freedom in Gravitational-Wave Detectors\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Essick%2C+R">Reed Essick</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Godwin%2C+P">Patrick Godwin</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Hanna%2C+C">Chad Hanna</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Blackburn%2C+L">Lindy Blackburn</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Katsavounidis%2C+E">Erik Katsavounidis</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 29 pages, 10 figures\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Instrumentation and Methods for Astrophysics (astro-ph.IM)</span>; General Relativity and Quantum Cosmology (gr-qc)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">Gravitational-wave detectors are exquisitely sensitive instruments and\nroutinely enable ground-breaking observations of novel astronomical phenomena.\nHowever, they also witness non-stationary, non-Gaussian noise that can be\nmistaken for astrophysical sources, lower detection confidence, or simply\ncomplicate the extraction of signal parameters from noisy data. To address\nthis, we present iDQ, a supervised learning framework to autonomously detect\nnoise artifacts in gravitational-wave detectors based only on auxiliary degrees\nof freedom insensitive to gravitational waves. iDQ has operated in low latency\nthroughout the advanced detector era at each of the two LIGO interferometers,\nproviding invaluable data quality information about each detection to date in\nreal-time. We document the algorithm, describing the statistical framework and\npossible applications within gravitational-wave searches. In particular, we\nconstruct a likelihood-ratio test that simultaneously accounts for the presence\nof non-Gaussian noise artifacts and utilizes information from both the observed\ngravitational-wave strain signal and thousands of auxiliary degrees of freedom.\nWe also present several examples of iDQ\'s performance with modern\ninterferometers, showing iDQ\'s ability to autonomously reproduce known data\nquality monitors and identify noise artifacts not flagged by other analyses.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item53">[53]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12767" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12767</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12767" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/ps/2005.12767" title="Download PostScript">ps</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12767" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Space VLBI 2020: Science and Technology Futures Conference Summary\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Lazio%2C+T+J+W">T. The\nfirst meeting (2018 September 5--6; Noordwijk, the Netherlands) focused on the\nfull range of science applications possible for very long baseline\ninterferometry (VLBI) with space-based antennas. Accordingly, the observing\nfrequencies (wavelengths) considered ranged from below 1~MHz (&gt; 300 m) to above\n300~GHz (&lt; 1 mm). For this second meeting, the focus was narrowed to mission\nconcepts and the supporting technologies to enable the highest angular\nresolution observations at frequencies of 30~GHz and higher (&lt; 1 cm).\n<br />This narrowing of focus was driven by both scientific and technical\nconsiderations. First, results from the RadioAstron mission and the Event\nHorizon Telescope (EHT) have generated considerable excitement for studying the\ninner portions of black hole (BH) accretion disks and jets and testing elements\nof the General Theory of Relativity (GR). Second, the technologies and\nrequirements involved in space-based VLBI differ considerably between 100~MHz\nand 100~GHz; a related consideration is that there are a number of existing\ninstruments or mission concepts for frequencies of approximately 100~MHz and\nbelow, while it has been some time since attention has been devoted to space\nVLBI at frequencies above 10~GHz.\n<br />This conference summary attempts to capture elements of presentations and\ndiscussions that occurred.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item54">[54]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12785" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12785</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12785" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12785" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Collisional heating and compaction of small bodies: Constraints for  their origin and evolution\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Jutzi%2C+M">Martin Jutzi</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Michel%2C+P">Patrick Michel</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 34 pages, 11 figures. However, how much small bodies were processed by past\ncollisions and to what extent they retain a record of processes that took place\nduring the formation and early evolution of the Solar System is still poorly\nunderstood. Here we study the degree of collisional heating and compaction by\nanalysing the large set of previous simulations of small body break-ups by\nJutzi et al. We have used the images recorded by the Atmospheric\nImaging Assembly and the Helioseismic Magnetic Imager on-board the Solar\nDynamics Observatory and spectroscopic observations taken from the\nExtreme-Ultraviolet Imaging Spectrometer on-board Hinode. The data from AIA 193\n{\\AA} channel show that TELs are formed between AR 12230 and a newly emerging\nAR 12234 and evolved during December 10-14, 2014. However, the brightest pixels have\nnon-thermal velocities of about 62 km/s for Fe XII and Fe XIII lines. Wimmer-Schweingruber</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Hauptmann%2C+M">Michael Hauptmann</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 11 pages, 7 figures\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Solar and Stellar Astrophysics (astro-ph.SR)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">Context. The potential field source surface model is frequently used as a\nbasis for further scientific investigations where a comprehensive coronal\nmagnetic field is of importance. Its parameters, especially the position and\nshape of the source surface, are crucial for the interpretation of the state of\nthe interplanetary medium. Improvements have been suggested that introduce one\nor more additional free parameters to the model, for example, the current sheet\nsource surface (CSSS) model.\n<br />Aims. Relaxing the spherical constraint of the source surface and allowing it\nto be elliptical gives modelers the option of deforming it to more accurately\nmatch the physical environment of the specific period or location to be\nanalyzed.\n<br />Methods. A numerical solver is presented that solves Laplace\'s equation on a\nthree-dimensional grid using finite differences. The solver is capable of\nworking on structured spherical grids that can be deformed to create elliptical\nsource surfaces.\n<br />Results. The configurations of the coronal magnetic field are presented using\nthis new solver. Three-dimensional renderings are complemented by\nCarrington-like synoptic maps of the magnetic configuration at different\nheights in the solar corona. Differences in the magnetic configuration computed\nby the spherical and elliptical models are illustrated.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item58">[58]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12854" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12854</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12854" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12854" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Spitzer Variability Properties of Low-Gravity L Dwarfs\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Vos%2C+J+M">Johanna M.
