Schlieder</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Brandner%2C+W">Wolfgang Brandner</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Henning%2C+T">Thomas Henning</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Bonavita%2C+M">Mariangela Bonavita</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Buenzli%2C+E">Esther Buenzli</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> Accepted for publication in AJ\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Solar and Stellar Astrophysics (astro-ph.SR)</span>; Earth and Planetary Astrophysics (astro-ph.EP)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">We present \\textit{Spitzer Space Telescope} variability monitoring\nobservations of three low-gravity L dwarfs with previous detections of\nvariability in the near-IR, 2MASS J0045+16, 2MASS J0501-00 and 2MASS J1425-36.\nWe detect significant, periodic variability in two of our targets, 2MASS\nJ0045+16 and 2MASS J0501-00. We do not detect variability in 2MASS J1425-36.\nCombining our new rotation periods with rotational velocities, we calculate\ninclination angles of $22\\pm1^{\\circ}$, ${60^{+13 }_{-8}} ^{\\circ}$ and\n$52^{+19}_{-13}~^{\\circ}$ for 2MASS J0045+16, 2MASS J0501-00 and 2MASS J1425-36\nrespectively. Our three new objects are consistent with the tentative relations\nbetween inclination, amplitude and color anomaly previously reported. Objects\nwith the highest variability amplitudes are inclined equator-on, while the\nmaximum observed amplitude decreases as the inclination angle decreases. We\nalso find a correlation between the inclination angle and\n$(J-K)_{\\mathrm{2MASS}}$ color anomaly for the sample of objects with measured\ninclinations. Compiling the entire sample of brown dwarfs with \\textit{Spitzer}\nvariability detections, we find no enhancement in amplitude for young, early-L\ndwarfs compared to the field dwarf population. We find a possible enhancement\nin amplitude of low-gravity late-L dwarfs at $4.5~\\mu$m. We do not find a\ncorrelation between amplitude ratio and spectral type for field dwarfs or for\nthe young population. Finally, we compile the rotation periods of a large\nsample of brown dwarfs with ages 1 Myr to 1 Gyr and compare the rotation rates\npredicted by evolutionary models assuming angular momentum conservation. We\nfind that the rotation rates of the current sample of brown dwarfs fall within\nthe expected range set by evolutionary models and breakup limits.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item59">[59]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12858" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12858</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12858" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12858" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> New multi-part collisional model of the main belt: The contribution to  near-Earth asteroids\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Zain%2C+P+S">P. S. Zain</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=de+El%C3%ADa%2C+G+C">G. C. de El&#xed;a</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Di+Sisto%2C+R+P">R. P. Di Sisto</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 14 pages, 12 Figures\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Earth and Planetary Astrophysics (astro-ph.EP)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">Aims. We developed a six-part collisional evolution model of the main\nasteroid belt (MB) and used it to study the contribution of the different\nregions of the MB to the near-earth asteroids (NEAs). Methods. We built a\nstatistical code called ACDC that simulates the collisional evolution of the MB\nsplit into six regions (namely Inner, Middle, Pristine, Outer, Cybele and\nHigh-Inclination belts) according to the positions of the major resonances\npresent there ($\\nu_{6}$, 3:1J, 5:2J, 7:3J and 2:1J). We consider the Yarkovsky\neffect and the mentioned resonances as the main mechanism that removes\nasteroids from the different regions of the MB and delivers them to the NEA\nregion. We calculated the evolution of the NEAs coming from the different\nsource regions by considering the bodies delivered by the resonances and mean\ndynamical timescales in the NEA population. Results. Our model is in agreement\nwith the major observational constraints associated with the MB, such as the\nsize distributions of the different regions of the MB and the number of large\nasteroid families. It is also able to reproduce the observed NEAs with H &lt; 16\nand agrees with recent estimations for H &lt; 20, but deviates for smaller sizes.\nWe find that most sources make a significant contribution to the NEAs; however\nthe Inner and Middle belts stand out as the most important source of NEAs\nfollowed by the Outer belt. The contributions of the Pristine and Cybele\nregions are minor. The High-Inclination belt is the source of only a fraction\nof the actual observed NEAs with high inclination, as there are dynamical\nprocesses in that region that enable asteroids to increase and decrease their\ninclinations.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item60">[60]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12867" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12867</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12867" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12867" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> A Systematic Study on the Absorption Features of Interstellar Ices in  Presence of Impurities\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Gorai%2C+P">Prasanta Gorai</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Sil%2C+M">Milan Sil</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Das%2C+A">Ankan Das</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Sivaraman%2C+B">Bhalamurugan Sivaraman</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Chakrabarti%2C+S+K">Sandip K. Some molecules have been identified\nwithin the interstellar ices either as pure, mixed, or even as layered\nstructures. Absorption band features of water ice can significantly change with\nthe presence of different types of impurities (CO, CO2, CH3OH, H2CO, etc.). In\nthis work, we carried out a theoretical investigation to understand the\nbehavior of water band frequency, and strength in the presence of impurities.\nThe computational study has been supported and complemented by some infrared\nspectroscopy experiments aimed at verifying the effect of HCOOH, NH3 , and CH3\nOH on the band profiles of pure H2O ice. Specifically, we explored the effect\non the band strength of libration, bending, bulk stretching, and free-OH\nstretching modes. Computed band strength profiles have been compared with our\nnew and existing experimental results, thus pointing out that vibrational modes\nof H2O and their intensities can change considerably in the presence of\nimpurities at different concentrations. In most cases, the bulk stretching mode\nis the most affected vibration, while the bending is the least affected mode.\nHCOOH was found to have a strong influence on the libration, bending, and bulk\nstretching band profiles. In the case of NH3, the free-OH stretching band\ndisappears when the impurity concentration becomes 50%. This work will\nultimately aid a correct interpretation of future detailed spaceborne\nobservations of interstellar ices by means of the upcoming JWST mission.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item61">[61]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12869" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12869</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12869" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12869" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Global X-Ray Properties of the Vela and Puppis A Supernova Remnants\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Silich%2C+E+M">E.M. Silich</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Kaaret%2C+P">P. Kaaret</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Zajczyk%2C+A">A. Bluem</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Ringuette%2C+R">R. Ringuette</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Jahoda%2C+K">K. Jahoda</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Kuntz%2C+K+D">K.D. Kuntz</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> accepted for publication in The Astronomical Journal, 8 pages, 4 figures\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">High Energy Astrophysical Phenomena (astro-ph.HE)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">The Vela and Puppis A supernova remnants (SNRs) comprise a large emission\nregion of $\\sim 8^{\\circ}$ diameter in the soft X-ray sky. The HaloSat CubeSat\nmission provides the first soft X-ray ($0.4-7$ keV) observation of the entire\nVela SNR and Puppis A SNR region with a single pointing and moderate spectral\nresolution. HaloSat observations of the Vela SNR are best fit with a\ntwo-temperature thermal plasma model consisting of a cooler component with\n$kT_{1} = 0.19^{+0.01}_{-0.01}$ keV in collisional ionization equilibrium and a\nhotter component with $kT_{2} = 1.06^{+0.45}_{-0.27}$ keV in non-equilibrium\nionization. Observations of the Puppis A SNR are best fit with a\nsingle-component plane-parallel shocked plasma model with $kT =\n0.86^{+0.06}_{-0.05}$ keV in non-equilibrium ionization. For the first time, we\nfind the total X-ray luminosities of both components of the Vela SNR spectrum\nin the $0.5-7$ keV energy band to be $L_X = 4.4^{+1.4}_{-1.4} \\times 10^{34}$\nerg s$^{-1}$ for the cooler component and $L_X = 4.1^{+1.8}_{-1.5} \\times\n10^{34}$ erg s$^{-1}$ for the hotter component. We find the total X-ray\nluminosities of the Vela and Puppis A SNRs to be $L_{\\text{X}} = 8.4 \\times\n10^{34}$ erg s$^{-1}$ and $L_X = 6.7^{+1.1}_{-0.9} \\times 10^{36}$ erg\ns$^{-1}$.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item62">[62]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12871" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12871</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12871" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12871" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Vortices evolution in the solar atmosphere: A dynamical equation for the  swirling strength\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Cuissa%2C+J+R+C">J.R. Canivete Cuissa</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Steiner%2C+O">O. Steiner</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 12 pages, to be published in A&amp;A\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Solar and Stellar Astrophysics (astro-ph.SR)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">We study vortex dynamics in the solar atmosphere by employing and deriving\nthe analytical evolution equations of two vortex identification criteria. The\ntwo criteria used are vorticity and the swirling strength. Vorticity can be\nbiased in the presence of shear flows, but its dynamical equation is well\nknown; the swirling strength is a more precise criterion for the identification\nof vortical flows, but its evolution equation is not known yet. Therefore, we\nexplore the possibility of deriving a dynamical equation for the swirling\nstrength. We then apply the two equations to analyze radiative MHD simulations\nof the solar atmosphere produced with the CO5BOLD code. We present a detailed\nreview of the swirling strength criterion and the mathematical derivation of\nits evolution equation. This equation did not exist in the literature before\nand it constitutes a novel tool that is suitable for the analysis of a wide\nrange of problems in (magneto-)hydrodynamics. By applying this equation to\nnumerical models, we find that hydrodynamical and magnetic baroclinicities are\nthe driving physical processes responsible for vortex generation in the\nconvection zone and the photosphere. Higher up in the chromosphere, the\nmagnetic terms alone dominate. Moreover, we find that the swirling strength is\nproduced at small scales in a chaotic fashion, especially inside magnetic flux\nconcentrations. The swirling strength represents an appropriate criterion for\nthe identification of vortices in turbulent flows, such as those in the solar\natmosphere. Moreover, its evolution equation, which is derived in this paper,\nis pivotal for obtaining precise information about the dynamics of these\nvortices and the physical mechanisms responsible for their production and\nevolution. Since this equation is available, the swirling strength is now the\nideal quantity to study the dynamics of vortices in (magneto-)hydrodynamics.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item63">[63]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12887" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12887</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12887" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/ps/2005.12887" title="Download PostScript">ps</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12887" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Dynamical History of the Uranian System\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=%C4%86uk%2C+M">Matija &#x106;uk</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Moutamid%2C+M+E">Maryame El Moutamid</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Tiscareno%2C+M+S">Matthew S. Tiscareno</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> Accepted for Planetary Science Journal\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Earth and Planetary Astrophysics (astro-ph.EP)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">We numerically simulate the past tidal evolution of the five large moons of\nUranus (Miranda, Ariel, Umbriel, Titania, and Oberon). We find that the most\nrecent major mean-motion resonance (MMR) between any two moons, the\nAriel-Umbriel 5:3 MMR, had a large effect on the whole system. Our results\nsuggest that this resonance is responsible for the current 4.3$^{\\circ}$\ninclination of Miranda (instead of previously proposed 3:1 Miranda-Umbriel\nMMR), and that all five moons had their inclinations excited during this\nresonance. Miranda experienced significant tidal heating during the\nAriel-Umbriel 5:3 MMR due to its eccentricity being excited by Ariel\'s secular\nperturbations. This tidal heating draws energy from shrinking of Miranda\'s\norbit, rather than Ariel\'s outward evolution, and can generate heat flows in\nexcess of 100 mW m$^{-2}$, sufficient to produce young coronae on Miranda. We\nfind that this MMR was followed by a sequence of secular resonances, which\nreshuffled the moons\' eccentricities and inclinations. We also find that the\nprecession of Oberon\'s spin axis is close to a resonance with the precession of\nUmbriel\'s orbital plane, and that this spin-orbit resonance was likely excited\nduring the Ariel-Umbriel 5:3 MMR. After the exit from the MMR, subsequent\nAriel-Umbriel secular resonance and Oberon-Umbriel spin-orbit resonance may be\nable to explain the current low inclinations of Ariel and Umbriel. The age of\nMiranda\'s surface features tentatively suggests Uranian tidal\n$Q=15,000-20,000$, which can be further refined in future work.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item64">[64]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12888" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12888</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12888" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12888" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Interactions among intermediate redshift galaxies. The case of  SDSSJ134420.86+663717.8\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Misquitta%2C+P">Persis Misquitta</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Bowles%2C+M">Micah Bowles</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Eckart%2C+A">Andreas Eckart</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Yttergren%2C+M">Madeleine Yttergren</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Busch%2C+G">Gerold Busch</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Valencia-S.%2C+M">Monica Valencia-S.</a>, \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Fazeli%2C+N">Nastaran Fazeli</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">Astrophysics of Galaxies (astro-ph.GA)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">We present the properties of the central supermassive black holes and the\nhost galaxies of the interacting object SDSSJ134420.86+663717.8. We obtained\noptical long slit spectroscopy data from the Large Binocular Telescope (LBT)\nusing the Multi Object Double Spectrograph (MODS). Analysing the spectra\nrevealed several strong broad and narrow emission lines of ionised gas in the\nnuclear region of one galaxy, whereas only narrow emission lines were visible\nfor the second galaxy. The optical spectra were used to plot diagnostic\ndiagrams, deduce rotation curves of the two galaxies, and calculate the masses\nof the central supermassive black holes. We find that the galaxy with broad\nemission line features has Seyfert~1 properties, while the galaxy with only\nnarrow emission line features seems to be star-forming in nature. Furthermore,\nwe find that the masses of the central supermassive black holes are almost\nequal at a few times 10^7 solar mass. Additionally, we present a simple N-body\nsimulation to shed some light on the initial conditions of the progenitor\ngalaxies. We find that for an almost orthogonal approach of the two interacting\ngalaxies, the model resembles the optical image of the system.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item65">[65]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12891" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12891</a> [<a href="/pdf/2005.12891" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/ps/2005.12891" title="Download PostScript">ps</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12891" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Dispersion measure components within host galaxies of Fast Radio Bursts:  observational constraints from statistical properties of FRBs\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/astro-ph?searchtype=author&query=Niino%2C+Y">Yuu Niino</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 13 pages, 10 figures, submitted to ApJ\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">High Energy Astrophysical Phenomena (astro-ph.HE)</span>\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">Dispersion measure (DM) of Fast Radio Bursts (FRBs) are commonly used as a\nindicator of distance assuming that DM in excess of the expected amount within\nthe Milky Way in the direction of each FRB arise mostly from the inter-galactic\nmedium. However, the assumption might not be true if, for example, most FRB\nprogenitors are embedded in ionized circumstellar material (CSM, e.g. supernova\nremnant). In this study, we jointly analyze distributions of DM, flux density,\nand fluence of the FRB samples observed by the Parkes telescope and the\nAustralian Square Kilometre Array Pathfinder (ASKAP) using analytical models of\nFRBs, to constrain fractions of various DM components that shape the overall DM\ndistribution and emission properties of FRBs. Comparing the model predictions\nwith the observations we find that the typical amount of DM in each FRB host\ngalaxy is $\\sim 120$ cm$^{-3}$pc which is naturally explained as a combination\nof interstellar medium (ISM) and halo of an ordinary galaxy, without additional\ncontribution from ionized CSM that is directly associated with an FRB\nprogenitor. Hertzberg</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 40 pages, 5 figures\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">General Relativity and Quantum Cosmology (gr-qc)</span>; Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics (astro-ph.CO); High Energy Physics - Phenomenology (hep-ph); High Energy Physics - Theory (hep-th); Quantum Physics (quant-ph)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">Decoherence describes the tendency of quantum sub-systems to dynamically lose\ntheir quantum character. This happens when the quantum sub-system of interest\ninteracts and becomes entangled with an environment that is traced out. For\nordinary macroscopic systems, electromagnetic and other interactions cause\nrapid decoherence. However, dark matter (DM) may have the unique possibility of\nexhibiting naturally prolonged macroscopic quantum properties due to its weak\ncoupling to its environment, particularly if it only interacts gravitationally.\nIn this work, we compute the rate of decoherence for light DM in the galaxy,\nwhere a local density has its mass, size, and location in a quantum\nsuperposition. The decoherence is via the gravitational interaction of the DM\noverdensity with its environment, provided by ordinary matter. We focus on\nrelatively robust configurations: DM perturbations that involve an overdensity\nfollowed by an underdensity, with no monopole, such that it is only observable\nat relatively close distances. We use non-relativistic scattering theory with a\nNewtonian potential generated by the overdensity to determine how a probe\nparticle scatters off of it and thereby becomes entangled. As an application,\nwe consider light scalar DM, including axions. In the galactic halo, we use\ndiffuse hydrogen as the environment, while near the earth, we use air as the\nenvironment. For an overdensity whose size is the typical DM de Broglie\nwavelength, we find that the decoherence rate in the halo is higher than the\npresent Hubble rate for DM masses $m_a \\lesssim 5 \\times 10^{-7}$eV and in\nearth based experiments it is higher than the classical field coherence rate\nfor $m_a \\lesssim 10^{-6}$eV. When spreading of the states occurs, the rates\ncan become much faster, as we quantify. Also, we establish that DM BECs\ndecohere very rapidly and so are very well described by classical field theory.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item71">[71]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12306" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12306</a> (cross-list from gr-qc) [<a href="/pdf/2005.12306" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12306" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Gravitational Waves Induced by Scalar Perturbations with a Lognormal  Peak\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/gr-qc?searchtype=author&query=Pi%2C+S">Shi Pi</a>, \n<a href="/search/gr-qc?searchtype=author&query=Sasaki%2C+M">Misao Sasaki</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 16 pages, 3 figures\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">General Relativity and Quantum Cosmology (gr-qc)</span>; Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics (astro-ph.CO); High Energy Physics - Theory (hep-th)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">We study the stochastic gravitational wave (GW) background induced by the\nprimordial scalar perturbation with the spectrum having a lognormal peak of\nwidth $\\Delta$ at $k=k_*$. The stability analysis is performed over a wide range\nof parameters of core and halo electron populations. Using the quasi-linear\nscaling relation we show that anti-parallel whistler waves saturate at\namplitudes of one order of magnitude smaller than parallel whistler waves,\nwhich is at about $10^{-3}\\;B_0$ in the pristine solar wind. The analysis shows\nthat the presence of anti-parallel whistler waves in the pristine solar wind is\nmore likely to be obscured by turbulent magnetic field fluctuations, because of\nlower frequencies and smaller amplitudes compared to parallel whistler waves.\nThe presented results will be also valuable for numerical simulations of the\nelectron heat flux regulation in the solar wind.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item75">[75]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12684" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12684</a> (cross-list from gr-qc) [<a href="/pdf/2005.12684" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/ps/2005.12684" title="Download PostScript">ps</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12684" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Big Rip: heating by Hawking radiation and a possible connection to  conformal cyclic cosmology\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/gr-qc?searchtype=author&query=Ruggiero%2C+R">Rafael Ruggiero</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 4 pages, 1 figure. To be submitted to Phys. Rev. D, comments welcome\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">General Relativity and Quantum Cosmology (gr-qc)</span>; Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics (astro-ph.CO)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">In the Big Rip cosmological scenario, a FRW universe containing dark energy\nwith $w &lt; -1$ in its equation of state (phantom energy) expands in such way\nthat, in a finite timespan, the scale factor diverges to infinity and the size\nof the cosmic horizon goes to zero. Here we revisit this scenario in light of\nthe fact that Hawking radiation is expected to be generated at the apparent\nhorizon of a FRW universe, and show that the energy density and temperature of\nthat radiation both diverge at the Big Rip. We then use this fact to propose a\nnew variant of Penrose\'s conformal cyclic cosmology model in which the future\nspacetime metric becomes conformally invariant at the Big Rip instead of in the\nremote future of a de Sitter universe; this removes the need for mass decay\nfrom the model and makes it consistent with current physical laws.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item76">[76]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12747" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12747</a> (cross-list from gr-qc) [<a href="/pdf/2005.12747" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/ps/2005.12747" title="Download PostScript">ps</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12747" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Transformation of Primordial Cosmological Perturbations Under the  General Extended Disformal Transformation\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/gr-qc?searchtype=author&query=Alinea%2C+A+L">Allan L. Alinea</a>, \n<a href="/search/gr-qc?searchtype=author&query=Kubota%2C+T">Takahiro Kubota</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 19 pages, for submission to JCAP\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">General Relativity and Quantum Cosmology (gr-qc)</span>; Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics (astro-ph.CO); High Energy Physics - Theory (hep-th)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">Primordial cosmological perturbations are the seeds that were cultivated by\ninflation and the succeeding dynamical processes, eventually leading to the\ncurrent Universe. In this work, we investigate the behaviour of the\ngauge-invariant scalar and tensor perturbations under the general extended\ndisformal transformation, namely, $g_{\\mu\\nu} \\rightarrow A(X,Y,Z)g_{\\mu\\nu} +\n\\Phi_\\mu\\Phi_\\nu$, where $X \\equiv -\\tfrac{1}{2}\\phi^{;\\mu}\\phi_{;\\mu}, Y\n\\equiv \\phi^{;\\mu}X_{;\\mu}, Z \\equiv X^{;\\mu}X_{;\\mu} $ and $\\Phi_\\mu \\equiv\nC\\phi_{;\\mu} + DX_{;\\mu}$, with $C$ and $D$ being a general functional of\n$(\\phi,X,Y,Z)$. We find that the tensor perturbation is invariant under this\ntransformation. On the other hand, the scalar curvature perturbation receives a\ncorrection due the conformal term only; it is independent of the disformal term\nat least up to linear order. Within the framework of the full Horndeski theory,\nthe correction terms turn out to depend linearly on the gauge-invariant\ncomoving density perturbation and the first time-derivative thereof. In the\nsuperhorizon limit, all these correction terms vanish, leaving only the\noriginal scalar curvature perturbation. In other words, it is invariant under\nthe general extended disformal transformation in the superhorizon limit, in the\ncontext of full Horndeski theory. Our work encompasses a chain of research\nstudies on the transformation or invariance of the primordial cosmological\nperturbations, generalising their results under our general extended disformal\ntransformation. Apart from the cosmological perturbations, this work and the\ntransformation considered herein, give us strong impetus to go beyond the\ncurrent horizon of scalar-tensor theories.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item77">[77]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12804" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12804</a> (cross-list from gr-qc) [<a href="/pdf/2005.12804" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/ps/2005.12804" title="Download PostScript">ps</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12804" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> Inflationary Attractors in $F(R)$ Gravity\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/gr-qc?searchtype=author&query=Odintsov%2C+S+D">S.D. Odintsov</a>, \n<a href="/search/gr-qc?searchtype=author&query=Oikonomou%2C+V+K">V.K. Oikonomou</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> PLB Accepted\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">General Relativity and Quantum Cosmology (gr-qc)</span>; Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics (astro-ph.CO); High Energy Physics - Theory (hep-th)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">In this letter we shall demonstrate that the viable $F(R)$ gravities can be\nclassified mainly into two classes of inflationary attractors, either the $R^2$\nattractors or the $\\alpha$-attractors. To show this, we shall derive the most\ngeneral relation between the tensor-to-scalar ratio $r$ and the spectral index\nof primordial curvature perturbations $n_s$, namely the $r-n_s$ relation, by\nassuming that the slow-roll condition constrains the values of the slow-roll\nindices. As we show, the relation between the tensor-to-scalar ratio and the\nspectral index of the primordial curvature perturbations has the form $r\\simeq\n\\frac{48 (1-n_s)^2}{(4-x)^2}$, where the dimensionless parameter $x$ contains\nhigher derivatives of the $F(R)$ gravity function with respect to the Ricci\nscalar, and it is a function of the $e$-foldings number $N$ and may also be a\nfunction of the free parameters of the various $F(R)$ gravity models. For\n$F(R)$ gravities which have a spectral index compatible with the observational\ndata and also yield $x\\ll 1$, these belong to the $R^2$-type of attractors,\nwith $r\\sim 3 (1-n_s)^2$, and these are viable theories. Moreover, in the case\nthat $x$ takes larger values in specific ranges and is constant for a given\n$F(R)$ gravity, the resulting $r-n_s$ relation has the form $r\\sim 3 \\alpha\n(1-n_s)^2$, where $\\alpha$ is a constant. Thus we conclude that the viable\n$F(R)$ gravities may be classified into two limiting types of $r-n_s$\nrelations, one identical to the $R^2$ model at leading order in $x$, and one\nsimilar to the $\\alpha$-attractors $r-n_s$ relation, for the $F(R)$ gravity\nmodels that yield $x$ constant. Finally, we also discuss the case that $x$ is\nnot constant.\n</p>\n</div>\n</dd>\n<dt><a name="item78">[78]</a>&nbsp;  <span class="list-identifier"><a href="/abs/2005.12808" title="Abstract">arXiv:2005.12808</a> (cross-list from hep-th) [<a href="/pdf/2005.12808" title="Download PDF">pdf</a>, <a href="/format/2005.12808" title="Other formats">other</a>]</span></dt>\n<dd>\n<div class="meta">\n<div class="list-title mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Title:</span> On catalyzed vacuum decay around a radiating black hole and the crisis  of the electroweak vacuum\n</div>\n<div class="list-authors">\n<span class="descriptor">Authors:</span> \n<a href="/search/hep-th?searchtype=author&query=Hayashi%2C+T">Takumi Hayashi</a>, \n<a href="/search/hep-th?searchtype=author&query=Kamada%2C+K">Kohei Kamada</a>, \n<a href="/search/hep-th?searchtype=author&query=Oshita%2C+N">Naritaka Oshita</a>, \n<a href="/search/hep-th?searchtype=author&query=Yokoyama%2C+J">Jun&#x27;ichi Yokoyama</a>\n</div>\n<div class="list-comments mathjax">\n<span class="descriptor">Comments:</span> 25 pages, 8 figures\n</div>\n<div class="list-subjects">\n<span class="descriptor">Subjects:</span> <span class="primary-subject">High Energy Physics - Theory (hep-th)</span>; Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics (astro-ph.CO); General Relativity and Quantum Cosmology (gr-qc); High Energy Physics - Phenomenology (hep-ph)\n\n</div>\n<p class="mathjax">False vacuum decay is a key feature in quantum field theories and exhibits a\ndistinct signature in the early Universe cosmology. It has recently been\nsuggested that the false vacuum decay is catalyzed by a black hole (BH), which\nmight cause the catastrophe of the Standard Model Higgs vacuum if primordial\nBHs are formed in the early Universe. We investigate vacuum phase transition of\na scalar field around a radiating BH with taking into account the effect of\nHawking radiation. We find that the vacuum decay rate slightly decreases in the\npresence of the thermal effect since the scalar potential is stabilized near\nthe horizon. However, the stabilization effect becomes weak at the points\nsufficiently far from the horizon.
